To enable the QoS cgroup hierarchy you need to specify a valid cgroup-root\")\n262: \t\t}\n263: \n264: \t\t// we need to check that the cgroup root actually exists for each subsystem\n265: \t\t// of note, we always use the cgroupfs driver when performing this check since\n266: \t\t// the input is provided in that format.\n267: \t\t// this is important because we do not want any name conversion to occur.\n268: \t\tif err := cgroupManager.Validate(cgroupRoot); err != nil {\n269: \t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"invalid configuration: %w\", err)\n270: \t\t}\n271: \t\tlogger.Info(\"Container manager verified user specified cgroup-root exists\", \"cgroupRoot\", cgroupRoot)\n272: \t\t// Include the top level cgroup for enforcing node allocatable into cgroup-root.\n273: \t\t// This way, all sub modules can avoid having to understand the concept of node allocatable.\n274: \t\tcgroupRoot = NewCgroupName(cgroupRoot, defaultNodeAllocatableCgroupName)\n275: \t}\n276: \tlogger.Info(\"Creating Container Manager object based on Node Config\", \"nodeConfig\", nodeConfig)\n277: \n278: \tqosContainerManager, err := NewQOSContainerManager(subsystems, cgroupRoot, nodeConfig, cgroupManager)\n279: \tif err != nil {\n280: \t\treturn nil, err\n281: \t}\n282: \n283: \tcm := &containerManagerImpl{\n284: \t\tcadvisorInterface:   cadvisorInterface,\n285: \t\tmountUtil:           mountUtil,\n286: \t\tNodeConfig:          nodeConfig,\n287: \t\tsubsystems:          subsystems,\n288: \t\tcgroupManager:       cgroupManager,\n289: \t\tcapacity:            capacity,\n290: \t\tinternalCapacity:    internalCapacity,\n291: \t\tcgroupRoot:          cgroupRoot,\n292: \t\trecorder:            recorder,\n293: \t\tqosContainerManager: qosContainerManager,\n294: \t}\n295: \n296: \tcm.topologyManager, err = topologymanager.NewManager(\n297: \t\tmachineInfo.Topology,\n298: \t\tnodeConfig.TopologyManagerPolicy,\n299: \t\tnodeConfig.TopologyManagerScope,\n300: \t\tnodeConfig.TopologyManagerPolicyOptions,\n301: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go%3FL1-300"}}}

Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe container manager is the core subsystem responsible for managing compute resource allocation, enforcement, and lifecycle on a node. It acts as the orchestration layer between the kubelet's pod synchronization logic and the underlying kernel resource control mechanisms (cgroups), container runtime (CRI), and specialized resource controllers.\n\n### Core Responsibilities\n- **Resource enforcement**: Apply CPU, memory, and device quotas to containers via cgroups\n- **Hierarchical QoS management**: Organize pods into Guaranteed, Burstable, and BestEffort cgroups\n- **Node allocatable enforcement**: Reserve resources for system and kubelet components\n- **Resource coordination**: Align CPU, memory, and device allocations with NUMA topology\n- **Plugin integration**: Manage device plugins and device memory allocation\n- **Dynamic resource lifecycle**: Support runtime preparation/unpreperation of extended resources (DRA)\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n- **Pod & Node APIs** (`k8s.io/api/core/v1`): Pod specifications, resource requests/limits, QoS class\n- **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)** (`k8s.io/cri-api`): Container lifecycle, resource updates\n- **cAdvisor** (`k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/kubelet/cadvisor`): Machine topology, capacity discovery\n- **Status Provider**: Pod status tracking from runtime\n- **Events**: Node event recording for warnings/errors\n\n### Downstream Dependencies\n- **Kubelet's pod workers** (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`): Trigger pod admission and synchronization\n- **Lifecycle admission handlers** (`pkg/kubelet/lifecycle`): Enforce pod admission constraints\n- **Pod resources API** (`pkg/kubelet/apis/podresources`): Expose allocated resources to external consumers\n- **Container runtime**: Actual container creation and resource enforcement\n- **cgroups filesystem**: Linux kernel resource limiting mechanism\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Separation\n\n### 2.1 ContainerManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go)\n\nThe primary interface implemented by `containerManagerImpl` defines the contract for all container management operations:\n\n```go\ntype ContainerManager interface {\n    Start(context.Context, *v1.Node, ActivePodsFunc, GetNodeFunc, ...) error\n    SystemCgroupsLimit() v1.ResourceList\n    GetNodeConfig() NodeConfig\n    Status() Status\n    NewPodContainerManager() PodContainerManager\n    GetMountedSubsystems() *CgroupSubsystems\n    GetQOSContainersInfo() QOSContainersInfo\n    GetNodeAllocatableReservation() v1.ResourceList\n    GetCapacity(localStorageCapacityIsolation bool) v1.ResourceList\n    UpdateQOSCgroups(logger klog.Logger) error\n    GetResources(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) (*RunContainerOptions, error)\n    GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler() lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler\n    InternalContainerLifecycle() InternalContainerLifecycle\n    PrepareDynamicResources(context.Context, *v1.Pod) error\n    UnprepareDynamicResources(context.Context, *v1.Pod) error\n    // ... additional methods for device tracking, exclusive CPUs, topology hints\n}\n```\n\n**Key responsibility**: Orchestrates initialization and maintains references to all sub-managers.\n\n### 2.2 containerManagerImpl (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go)\n\nThe Linux-specific implementation manages the lifecycle and coordination of six core sub-systems:\n\n| Component | Role | File |\n|-----------|------|------|\n| **CgroupManager** | Abstracts cgroup v1/v2 operations (create, update, destroy cgroups) | `cgroup_manager_linux.go` |\n| **QOSContainerManager** | Creates and maintains QoS-tier cgroup hierarchy | `qos_container_manager_linux.go` |\n| **CPU Manager** | Allocates CPU affinity based on policy (static/none) | `cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` |\n| **Memory Manager** | Allocates NUMA-local memory for guaranteed pods | `memorymanager/memory_manager.go` |\n| **Device Manager** | Manages device plugin allocations | `devicemanager/manager.go` |\n| **Topology Manager** | Coordinates NUMA-aware resource alignment | `topologymanager/topology_manager.go` |\n| **DRA Manager** | Handles Dynamic Resource Allocation (optional feature) | `dra/manager.go` |\n\n**State in containerManagerImpl**:\n```go\ntype containerManagerImpl struct {\n    sync.RWMutex\n    NodeConfig                      // Configuration: cgroup paths, policies, limits\n    cadvisorInterface               // Machine topology and capacity discovery\n    cgroupManager CgroupManager      // Low-level cgroup operations\n    qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager\n    deviceManager devicemanager.Manager\n    cpuManager cpumanager.Manager\n    memoryManager memorymanager.Manager\n    topologyManager topologymanager.Manager\n    draManager *dra.Manager\n    capacity, internalCapacity v1.ResourceList\n    cgroupRoot CgroupName            // Root cgroup for all pods\n    systemContainers []*systemContainer  // Kubelet, system services\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 PodContainerManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go)\n\nAbstracts pod-level cgroup management, enabling the two-tier hierarchy (QoS tier → pod tier → container tier):\n\n```go\ntype PodContainerManager interface {\n    GetPodContainerName(*v1.Pod) (CgroupName, string)\n    EnsureExists(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\n    Exists(*v1.Pod) bool\n    Destroy(logger klog.Logger, name CgroupName) error\n    ReduceCPULimits(logger klog.Logger, name CgroupName) error\n    GetAllPodsFromCgroups() (map[types.UID]CgroupName, error)\n    IsPodCgroup(cgroupfs string) (bool, types.UID)\n    GetPodCgroupMemoryUsage(pod *v1.Pod) (uint64, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation**: `podContainerManagerImpl` (pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go)\n- Maps pod UID → cgroup under appropriate QoS tier\n- Creates pod cgroup during pod admission\n- Configures CPU/memory QoS parameters per pod\n\n### 2.4 Resource Managers\n\n#### CPU Manager (pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go)\n\n**Purpose**: Allocate exclusive CPUs to containers requesting them.\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Start(ctx context.Context, activePods ActivePodsFunc, sourcesReady config.SourcesReady,\n          podStatusProvider status.PodStatusProvider, containerRuntime runtimeService,\n          initialContainers containermap.ContainerMap) error\n    Allocate(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) error\n    AddContainer(logger logr.Logger, p *v1.Pod, c *v1.Container, containerID string)\n    RemoveContainer(logger logr.Logger, containerID string) error\n    State() state.Reader\n    GetTopologyHints(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n    GetExclusiveCPUs(podUID, containerName string) cpuset.CPUSet\n    GetAllocatableCPUs() cpuset.CPUSet\n}\n```\n\n**Policies**:\n- **None** (`policy_none.go`): No CPU pinning; all containers share the shared pool\n- **Static** (`policy_static.go`): Exclusive CPU allocation with optional NUMA/socket alignment\n\n**State persistence**: Checkpointed to `cpu_manager_state` file (kubelet root dir)\n\n#### Memory Manager (pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go)\n\n**Purpose**: Allocate NUMA-local memory to guaranteed pods.\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Start(ctx context.Context, activePods ActivePodsFunc, sourcesReady config.SourcesReady,\n          podStatusProvider status.PodStatusProvider, containerRuntime runtimeService,\n          initialContainers containermap.ContainerMap) error\n    AddContainer(logger klog.Logger, p *v1.Pod, c *v1.Container, containerID string)\n    Allocate(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) error\n    RemoveContainer(logger klog.Logger, containerID string) error\n    State() state.Reader\n    GetTopologyHints(*v1.Pod, *v1.Container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n    GetMemoryNUMANodes(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) sets.Set[int]\n    GetAllocatableMemory() []state.Block\n}\n```\n\n**Policies**:\n- **None**: No special memory allocation\n- **Static**: Allocates memory from isolated NUMA nodes per container, only for guaranteed containers\n\n#### Device Manager (pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/)\n\n**Purpose**: Enumerate device plugins, allocate devices to containers, collect topology hints.\n\n**Key methods**:\n- `Start(ctx)`: Discover and manage device plugin endpoints\n- `Allocate(ctx, pod, container) error`: Call device plugin Allocate RPC\n- `GetDeviceRunContainerOptions(ctx, pod, container)`: Return CDI devices, mounts, envs for runtime\n- `GetTopologyHints(pod, container)`: Provide NUMA alignment hints\n- `UpdateAllocatedDevices()`: Release devices from terminated pods\n\n**Device plugins** communicate via Unix socket following the Kubernetes device plugin protocol.\n\n#### Topology Manager (pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/)\n\n**Purpose**: Coordinate NUMA topology hints from CPU, memory, and device managers during pod admission.\n\n**Policies**:\n- **None**: No topology awareness (default)\n- **Best-Effort**: Collect hints but allow pod admission regardless\n- **Restricted**: Reject pod if no topology hint can satisfy all managers\n- **Single-NUMA-Node**: Reject pod if resources cannot be allocated from a single NUMA node\n\n**Admission flow**:\n1. Pod admission handler calls `Admit(pod, attributes)`\n2. Topology manager queries `GetTopologyHints(pod, container)` for each manager\n3. Evaluates policy and either approves or rejects the pod\n\n### 2.5 CgroupManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go, cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go, cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go)\n\n**Purpose**: Abstract cgroup v1 vs. v2 implementation differences.\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype CgroupManager interface {\n    Create(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Destroy(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Update(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Exists(name CgroupName) bool\n    Pids(logger klog.Logger, name CgroupName) []int\n    MemoryUsage(name CgroupName) (int64, error)\n    Version() int  // 1 or 2\n}\n```\n\n**CgroupConfig** specifies:\n```go\ntype CgroupConfig struct {\n    Name CgroupName  // e.g., []string{\"kubepods\", \"burstable\", \"pod-abc-123\"}\n    ResourceParameters *ResourceConfig\n}\n```\n\n**ResourceConfig** holds:\n- Memory limit (bytes)\n- CPU set (pinning)\n- CPU shares (relative weight)\n- CPU quota/period (CFS bandwidth limiting)\n- PIDs limit\n- Cgroup v2 unified dict for memory QoS, etc.\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Container Manager Initialization\n\n**File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:NewContainerManager()` (line 207)**\n\n```\n1. Validate cgroup subsystems mounted (cpu, memory, cpuset at minimum)\n   ↓\n2. Get machine info from cAdvisor (topology, capacity)\n   ↓\n3. Create CgroupManager (v1 or v2 driver)\n   ↓\n4. Validate and set cgroup root (e.g., /kubepods)\n   ↓\n5. Create QOSContainerManager\n   └─ Initializes three QoS tier cgroups:\n      - guaranteed: high priority, strict isolation\n      - burstable: medium priority, shared CPU shares\n      - besteffort: low priority, shared resources\n   ↓\n6. Create Topology Manager (with policy)\n   ↓\n7. Create Device Manager\n   ├─ Scan /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins for sockets\n   └─ Establish watch connection for device updates\n   ↓\n8. Create CPU Manager (with policy and reserved CPUs)\n   └─ Reconciliation loop monitors container CPU affinity\n   ↓\n9. Create Memory Manager (with policy and NUMA info)\n   └─ Tracks memory allocation state for guaranteed pods\n   ↓\n10. Register CPU/Memory/Device as Topology Manager hint providers\n   ↓\n11. Create resource updates channel\n    └─ Fan-in updates from device and DRA managers\n```\n\n**Result**: `containerManagerImpl` ready for `Start()` call during kubelet startup.\n\n### 3.2 Pod Admission Flow\n\n**Trigger**: Kubelet receives new pod; calls `NewLifecycleManager().Admit(pod, attributes)`\n\n**File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` (line 760)**\nReturns `topologyManager` as the admission handler.\n\n**Flow**:\n\n```\nPod arrives at kubelet\n   ↓\n→ Topology Manager Admit()\n   ├─ For each container in pod:\n   │  ├─ Call CPU Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n   │  ├─ Call Memory Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n   │  └─ Call Device Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n   │\n   ├─ Apply topology policy:\n   │  ├─ Collect hints from all managers\n   │  ├─ Find best alignment (if restricted policy)\n   │  └─ Reject pod if no alignment possible (restricted/single-numa-node)\n   │\n   └─ If approved:\n      ├─ Pod advances to pod worker\n      └─ Pod worker calls Allocate() during SyncPod\n   ↓\n→ Pod Worker SyncPod()\n   └─ Calls containerManager.GetResources() per container\n      ├─ DRA Manager.GetResources(pod, container) → CDI devices\n      └─ Device Manager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions(pod, container)\n         → Devices, Mounts, Env vars, Annotations, CDI devices\n   ↓\n→ Resource Allocation Calls\n   ├─ CPU Manager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   │  └─ State: Record (pod UID, container name) → CPUSet\n   ├─ Memory Manager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   │  └─ State: Record pod UID → NUMA node allocation\n   └─ Device Manager.Allocate(pod, container)\n      └─ RPC to device plugin: AllocateRequest → AllocateResponse\n   ↓\n→ Container Creation\n   └─ Runtime receives RunContainerOptions with allocated resources\n      ├─ CPU affinity set via CRI ContainerConfig\n      ├─ Devices passed via RunOptions\n      └─ Env vars injected for device paths\n```\n\n### 3.3 Container Lifecycle Management\n\n**File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`**\n\nThe `InternalContainerLifecycle` provides hooks called at critical points:\n\n```\nContainer being created\n   ↓\n→ InternalContainerLifecycle.PreCreateContainer()\n   ├─ Called during CreateContainer in kuberuntime\n   └─ Not currently used for resource managers\n   ↓\n→ Container created successfully\n   ↓\n→ InternalContainerLifecycle.PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   ├─ CPU Manager.AddContainer(logger, pod, container, containerID)\n   │  └─ Maps containerID → (pod UID, container name) for later reconciliation\n   ├─ Memory Manager.AddContainer(logger, pod, container, containerID)\n   │  └─ Registers container in memory allocation tracking\n   └─ Topology Manager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n      └─ Registers container for topology state tracking\n   ↓\n→ Container runs\n   ↓\n→ Container terminated\n   ↓\n→ InternalContainerLifecycle.PostStopContainer(containerID)\n   └─ Topology Manager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      └─ Cleanup topology state\n   ↓\n→ Background: CPU/Memory managers remove container during reconciliation\n   ├─ CPU Manager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n   │  └─ Release CPUs back to shared pool\n   └─ Memory Manager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      └─ Release NUMA node allocations\n```\n\n### 3.4 QoS Cgroup Hierarchy Creation\n\n**File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:setupNode()` (line 504)**\n\nDuring `Start()`, if `CgroupsPerQOS` is enabled:\n\n```\nStart()\n   ↓\n→ setupNode(ctx, activePods)\n   ├─ Validate cgroup subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset, etc.)\n   ├─ Setup kernel tunables (sysctl)\n   ├─ createNodeAllocatableCgroups()\n   │  └─ Create cgroup under user-specified cgroup-root\n   │     └─ (e.g., /kubepods under /sys/fs/cgroup/)\n   │\n   ├─ qosContainerManager.Start()\n   │  └─ Create three QoS tier cgroups\n   │     ├─ /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/.../kubepods/guaranteed\n   │     ├─ /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/.../kubepods/burstable\n   │     └─ /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/.../kubepods/besteffort\n   │\n   ├─ enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()\n   │  └─ Set limits on each QoS tier based on:\n   │     ├─ Node capacity\n   │     ├─ Node allocatable\n   │     └─ QoS reserved settings\n   │\n   └─ Setup system containers (Kubelet, system services)\n      └─ Ensure kubelet process in designated cgroup\n```\n\n**Cgroup hierarchy structure**:\n```\n/kubepods                                     # Node allocatable enforcement\n├─ guaranteed/                                # Guaranteed pods\n│  └─ pod-<uid>/                              # Individual pod\n│     ├─ <container1>/                        # Individual container\n│     └─ <container2>/\n├─ burstable/\n│  └─ pod-<uid>/\n│     └─ <containers>/\n└─ besteffort/\n   └─ pod-<uid>/\n      └─ <containers>/\n```\n\n### 3.5 Pod Synchronization (SyncPod)\n\n**Simplified flow during pod worker's SyncPod() call:**\n\n```\nSyncPod(pod)\n   ↓\n→ Ensure pod container created\n   ├─ Get PodContainerManager from containerManager\n   │  (returns podContainerManagerImpl)\n   │\n   ├─ podContainerManager.EnsureExists(pod)\n   │  ├─ Determine pod QoS class (Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort)\n   │  ├─ Get parent QoS cgroup (guaranteed/burstable/besteffort)\n   │  └─ Create pod cgroup under parent:\n   │     └─ cgroupManager.Create(logger, &CgroupConfig{\n   │        Name: NewCgroupName(parentQoS, \"pod-<uid>\"),\n   │        ResourceParameters: ResourceConfigForPod(pod, ...),\n   │     })\n   │     ├─ CPU limits: Based on requests and CPU manager policy\n   │     ├─ Memory limits: Based on memory requests\n   │     └─ CPU/Memory QoS params: If MemoryQoS feature enabled\n   │\n   └─ For each container in pod:\n      ├─ Allocate resources (CPU, memory, devices)\n      ├─ Get container runtime options\n      │  └─ containerManager.GetResources(ctx, pod, container)\n      │     ├─ draManager.GetResources() → CDI devices\n      │     └─ deviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions() → Devices/Mounts/Env\n      │\n      └─ Create container with runtime\n         └─ Container runtime applies:\n            ├─ CPU affinity (from CPU Manager)\n            ├─ Memory limits and NUMA policy\n            ├─ Device mounts and CDI devices\n            └─ Environment variables from device manager\n```\n\n### 3.6 Resource Reconciliation\n\n**CPU Manager Reconciliation** (runs periodically):\n\n```\nEvery CPUManagerReconcilePeriod (default: 200ms)\n   ↓\n→ cpuManager reconciles current state\n   ├─ Get active pods from activePods()\n   ├─ For each running container:\n   │  ├─ Read desired CPU set from state\n   │  ├─ Get actual CPU set from cgroup (cpuset.cpus)\n   │  ├─ If mismatch:\n   │  │  └─ Update via runtimeService.UpdateContainerResources()\n   │  │     └─ CRI call to container runtime to apply CPU affinity\n   │  └─ Update container's CPU period/quota if needed\n   │\n   └─ Enforce allocatable reservation (reserved CPUs stay isolated)\n```\n\n**Memory Manager Reconciliation**:\n```\nOn startup and periodically\n   ↓\n→ memoryManager reconciles\n   ├─ Load state from checkpoint file (memory_manager_state)\n   ├─ For each running guaranteed pod:\n   │  └─ Verify memory allocation matches state\n   │\n   └─ Call runtimeService.UpdateContainerResources() if needed\n      └─ Apply memory limits and NUMA policies\n```\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n| Scenario | Impact | Mitigation |\n|----------|--------|-----------|\n| **Cgroup subsystem not mounted** | Container manager fails to initialize | Kubelet startup error; operator must enable cgroups |\n| **Swap enabled on node** | Memory limits not enforced; pod eviction may fail | `--fail-swap-on=true` (default) prevents kubelet start, or warning issued |\n| **CPU quota period unsupported** | CPU hardcapping unavailable | Status.SoftRequirements reports error; kubelet still starts |\n| **Device plugin crashes** | Containers can't allocate devices | Device allocation fails; pod admission rejected if devices required |\n| **NUMA topology detection fails** | Topology manager can't provide hints | Topology manager reverts to \"none\" policy; pod admission succeeds without alignment |\n| **Cgroup v1 to v2 migration** | Old state not readable in new hierarchy | CPUManager/MemoryManager state files incompatible; state must be cleared |\n| **Container removed without notification** | Resource leak (CPUs, memory, devices) | Periodic reconciliation detects orphaned resources and cleans up |\n| **Kubelet restart while pod running** | State loss; resources may be re-allocated | Checkpoints persisted to disk; restored on startup |\n\n### 4.2 Resource Limits and Constraints\n\n| Limit | Default | Tunable | Impact |\n|-------|---------|---------|--------|\n| **Pod PIDs limit** | Unbounded | `--pod-pids-limit` | Prevents fork bombs at pod level |\n| **CPU CFS quota period** | 100ms | `--cpu-cfs-quota-period` | Too low: scheduler overhead; too high: coarse granularity |\n| **CPU Manager reconcile period** | 200ms | `--cpu-manager-reconcile-period` | Tradeoff between responsiveness and overhead |\n| **Topology Manager scope** | container | `--topology-manager-scope=pod` | Pod scope: stricter alignment but higher rejection rate |\n| **Device manager max devices per pod** | No hard limit | Plugin-dependent | Device availability is soft limit |\n| **Memory allocatable reservation** | Computed from allocatable | Per-NUMA manual reservation | Prevents overallocation on NUMA nodes |\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### 3.3.1 Stateful Resource Allocation vs. Runtime State\n\n**Tradeoff**: CPU and Memory managers maintain state on disk (checkpoint files).\n- **Advantage**: Survive kubelet restart; container resources not lost\n- **Disadvantage**: State can become stale; requires garbage collection on pod cleanup\n- **Evidence**: `cpu_manager_state`, `memory_manager_state` files in kubelet root directory\n\n#### 3.3.2 Topology Hints vs. Hard NUMA Binding\n\n**Tradeoff**: Topology manager collects hints; final NUMA decision made during runtime.UpdateContainerResources().\n- **Advantage**: Resource managers can express preferences; runtime (e.g., containerd) applies best policy\n- **Disadvantage**: Hints can be ignored by runtime; containers may not get optimal NUMA locality\n- **Evidence**: `topologymanager/policy_*.go` provide hints; CPU/Memory managers don't directly set NUMA masks\n\n#### 3.3.3 Per-Pod vs. Per-Container Resource Management\n\n**Tradeoff**: Kubelet enforces pod-level cgroup limits; per-container limits via cgroup limits.\n- **Advantage**: Pod-level QoS applies across all containers; simpler admission\n- **Disadvantage**: Container-level oversubscription possible (e.g., 2 containers each requesting 500m CPU in 1CPU pod)\n- **Evidence**: `podContainerManagerImpl.EnsureExists()` creates pod cgroup; CPUs allocated per-container\n\n#### 3.3.4 Exclusive CPU Allocation and Shared Pool\n\n**Tradeoff**: Static CPU policy allocates exclusive CPUs to some containers; others share.\n- **Advantage**: Deterministic latency for latency-sensitive workloads (exclusive)\n- **Disadvantage**: CPU fragmentation; shared pool may be underutilized or overloaded\n- **Evidence**: `cpumanager/policy_static.go` tracks exclusive set; others use shared pool\n\n#### 3.3.5 Device Plugin Protocol vs. Built-in Device Support\n\n**Tradeoff**: Devices managed via out-of-process plugins (Unix sockets).\n- **Advantage**: Extensibility; new device types without kubelet changes\n- **Disadvantage**: Plugin crashes impact availability; state not persisted in kubelet\n- **Evidence**: Device manager scans `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/` for sockets; allocations stored in memory only\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Policy Customization\n\n#### CPU Manager Policies\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go`\n\nImplement `Policy` interface:\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start(cpuDetails CPUDetails, systemReserved, kubeReserved cpuset.CPUSet) error\n    AddContainer(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container, containerID string) error\n    RemoveContainer(containerID string) error\n    GetExclusiveCPUs(podUID, containerName string) cpuset.CPUSet\n    GetTopologyHints(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n}\n```\n\n**Builtin policies**:\n- `policy_none.go`: All containers share CPUs\n- `policy_static.go`: Guaranteed pods with integer CPU requests get exclusive CPUs\n\n**Extension**: Add new policy by implementing `Policy` interface and registering in `NewManager()` switch statement.\n\n#### Memory Manager Policies\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy.go`\n\nImplement `Policy` interface:\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start(guaranteedPods []*v1.Pod) error\n    AddContainer(logger logr.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container, containerID string) error\n    RemoveContainer(logger logr.Logger, containerID string) error\n    GetTopologyHints(...) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n}\n```\n\n**Builtin policies**:\n- `policy_none.go`: No memory pinning\n- `policy_static.go`: NUMA-local allocation for guaranteed pods\n\n#### Topology Manager Policies\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy.go`\n\nImplement `Manager` interface (admission, hint aggregation).\n\n**Builtin policies**:\n- `policy_none.go`: No topology awareness\n- `policy_best_effort.go`: Collect hints but allow pod regardless\n- `policy_restricted.go`: Reject pod if hints don't align\n- `policy_single_numa_node.go`: Restrict to single NUMA node\n\n### 5.2 Topology Manager Hint Provider Registration\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:NewContainerManager()` (line 296–356)\n\nAny component implementing `topologymanager.HintProvider` can register:\n\n```go\ncm.topologyManager.AddHintProvider(logger, deviceManager)\ncm.topologyManager.AddHintProvider(logger, cpuManager)\ncm.topologyManager.AddHintProvider(logger, memoryManager)\n```\n\n**How to add new provider**:\n1. Implement `GetTopologyHints(pod, container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint`\n2. Call `topologyManager.AddHintProvider()` in container manager initialization\n3. Topology manager queries your provider during pod admission\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugin Integration\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/`\n\nDevice plugins communicate via gRPC over Unix socket:\n\n```protobuf\nservice DevicePlugin {\n    rpc ListAndWatch(Empty) returns (stream ListAndWatchResponse);\n    rpc Allocate(AllocateRequest) returns (AllocateResponse);\n    rpc PreStartContainer(PreStartContainerRequest) returns (PreStartContainerResponse);\n    rpc GetDeviceRunContainerOptions(GetDeviceRunContainerOptionsRequest) returns (GetDeviceRunContainerOptionsResponse);\n    rpc GetPreferredAllocation(GetPreferredAllocationRequest) returns (GetPreferredAllocationResponse);\n}\n```\n\n**Extension**: Write a device plugin that listens on `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/<plugin_name>.sock` and implements the protocol.\n\n### 5.4 Runtime Service Updates\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`, `memorymanager/memory_manager.go`\n\nManagers call:\n```go\nruntimeService.UpdateContainerResources(ctx, containerID, &runtimeapi.ContainerResources{\n    CPUPeriod: period,\n    CPUQuota:  quota,\n    CPUSetCpus: cpuSetStr,\n    MemoryLimitInBytes: memLimit,\n    MemorySwapLimitInBytes: swapLimit,\n    // ... other fields\n})\n```\n\n**Extension**: Kubelet's runtime interface supports any CRI-compatible runtime (containerd, cri-o, etc.). Resource updates are propagated to the runtime, which applies them to the container.\n\n### 5.5 Kubelet's Pod Admit Handler Chain\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/admission.go`\n\nContainer manager's `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns the topology manager, which is consulted during pod admission:\n\n```go\nhandlers := []lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler{\n    cm.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler(), // Topology manager\n    // ... other handlers (secrets, volumes, etc.)\n}\n```\n\n**Extension**: Custom admission handlers can be registered in the kubelet's admission chain (outside container manager scope, but coordinates with it).\n\n## 6. Platform Variance\n\n### 6.1 Linux vs. Windows\n\n**Linux**: Full cgroup-based resource enforcement via containerManagerImpl (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go)\n- Cgroups v1 and v2 support\n- CPU manager and memory manager support\n- QoS cgroup hierarchy\n- NUMA and device topology support\n\n**Windows**: Minimal stub implementation (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go)\n- No cgroup support (Windows uses Job Objects instead)\n- CPU/memory managers still initialized but operate on Job Object limits\n- Topology manager and device manager functional\n- No QoS cgroup hierarchy\n\n### 6.2 Cgroup v1 vs. v2\n\n**Cgroup v1** (legacy):\n- Separate subsystems: cpu, cpuacct, memory, cpuset, pids\n- Kubelet validates each subsystem mounted\n- Files: cpu.shares, cpu.cfs_quota_us, memory.limit_in_bytes, cpuset.cpus\n\n**Cgroup v2** (unified):\n- Single hierarchy with all controllers\n- Kubelet detects via `cgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode()`\n- Files: cpu.max, memory.max, cpuset.cpus\n- Automatic memory QoS via memory.oom.group and memory.pressure_level\n\n**Handling**: CgroupManager abstraction hides v1/v2 differences\n- `cgroup_manager_linux.go`: Detects version\n- `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`: v1-specific logic\n- `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`: v2-specific logic\n\n### 6.3 CPU Hard Capping\n\n**Feature flag**: `CPUHardcapping`\n\nIf CPU CFS quota unavailable (old kernel or cgroup v1 cpu subsystem missing):\n- Kubelet detects during `validateSystemRequirements()`\n- Sets `status.SoftRequirements` error\n- Kubelet still starts but CPU limits not enforced\n- Users must manually manage CPU affinity\n\n### 6.4 Memory QoS\n\n**Feature flag**: `MemoryQoS` (requires cgroup v2)\n\n**Behavior**:\n```go\nif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(kubefeatures.MemoryQoS) &&\n   libcontainercgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode() {\n    // Apply memory QoS parameters\n    // E.g., memory.min, memory.low, memory.oom.group\n}\n```\n\nOptimizes OOM behavior for guaranteed vs. burstable pods.\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance Considerations\n\n#### CPU Manager Overhead\n- Reconciliation runs every `cpu-manager-reconcile-period` (default 200ms)\n- Cost: Iterating active pods, reading cgroup state, CRI UpdateContainerResources() calls\n- Mitigation: Set reconciliation period based on workload sensitivity (higher period for batch workloads)\n\n#### Topology Manager Admission Latency\n- Pod admission time increases with number of containers and NUMA nodes\n- Complexity grows in `restricted` and `single-numa-node` policies\n- Mitigation: Use `best-effort` for large clusters; reserve topology-sensitive pods for dedicated nodes\n\n#### Device Manager Scalability\n- Device plugins communicate synchronously with kubelet\n- Large number of devices per container → longer Allocate() RPC time\n- Mitigation: Device plugins should implement PreferredAllocation() to minimize allocation rounds\n\n### 7.2 Reliability and Recovery\n\n#### Checkpoint Persistence\n- CPU and Memory managers write state to disk after each change\n- **Location**: `${kubelet-root-dir}/cpu_manager_state`, `memory_manager_state`\n- **Recovery**: On kubelet restart, state is restored from checkpoint\n- **Risk**: If checkpoint corrupted, manually delete and kubelet will re-allocate from runtime state\n\n#### Orphaned Resource Cleanup\n- If container dies without notifying kubelet, resources may be allocated in cgroup but not tracked\n- **Detection**: Periodic reconciliation compares runtime pods with cgroup state\n- **Cleanup**: Garbage collection removes resources from orphaned cgroups\n\n#### Device Plugin Tolerance\n- If device plugin crashes, existing pod allocations persisted in kubelet state\n- New pods cannot allocate from crashed plugin\n- **Recovery**: Restart device plugin; kubelet re-establishes connection\n\n### 7.3 Monitoring and Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics\n- `kubelet_cgroup_manager_duration_seconds`: Time to create/update cgroups\n- `kubelet_pod_worker_duration_seconds`: Pod synchronization time (includes resource allocation)\n- `kubelet_device_manager_alloc_duration_seconds`: Device allocation latency\n- `kubelet_cpu_manager_reconcile_duration_seconds`: CPU manager reconciliation time\n\n#### Logs to Monitor\n- Look for \"Failed to allocate CPU\" → CPU exhaustion or allocation errors\n- Look for \"topology manager policy violation\" → Pod rejected due to NUMA constraints\n- Look for \"device plugin endpoint not found\" → Device plugin startup issues\n\n### 7.4 Configuration Best Practices\n\n| Setting | Recommendation | Rationale |\n|---------|-----------------|-----------|\n| `--cpu-manager-policy=static` | Only for latency-sensitive workloads | Overhead is minimal; helps predictable latency |\n| `--memory-manager-policy=static` | Only if NUMA allocation critical | Adds memory pinning overhead |\n| `--topology-manager-policy=restricted` | For co-located workloads needing alignment | Restrictive; use `best-effort` for flexibility |\n| `--pod-pids-limit=4096` | Set per node based on workload | Prevents fork bombs; reduce for untrusted multi-tenant |\n| `--cgroups-per-qos=true` | Recommended for multi-tenant clusters | Enables QoS isolation; always enable |\n| `--enforce-node-allocatable=pods,kube-reserved,system-reserved` | Strict enforcement | Prevents kubelet/system starvation |\n\n## 8. File and Directory Reference Map\n\n### Core Container Manager\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` | ContainerManager interface definition |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` | Linux implementation; initialization, lifecycle, orchestration |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` | Windows stub implementation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` | Shared types: CgroupConfig, ResourceConfig, PodContainerManager |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` | Pod-level cgroup management |\n\n### Cgroup Management\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` | Main cgroup manager; driver selection |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` | Cgroup v1 operations |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` | Cgroup v2 operations |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` | QoS tier cgroup creation/management |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/node_container_manager_linux.go` | Node-level cgroup enforcement |\n\n### Resource Managers\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` | CPU allocation interface and manager implementation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy*.go` | CPU allocation policies (none, static) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/state/` | CPU allocation state persistence |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go` | Memory allocation interface and manager |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy*.go` | Memory allocation policies (none, static) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go` | Device plugin integration |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go` | NUMA topology coordination |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy*.go` | Topology policies (none, best-effort, restricted, single-numa-node) |\n\n### Lifecycle Hooks\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` | Hooks for container lifecycle (PreStart, PostStop) |\n\n### DRA (Dynamic Resource Allocation)\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/` | Dynamic resource allocation manager |\n\n### Interfaces and Contracts\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go` | Runtime interface (pod/container status, lifecycle) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/` | Pod admission lifecycle hooks |\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe kubelet container manager is a layered architecture orchestrating resource allocation through six specialized sub-systems (CPU, Memory, Device, Topology, DRA, QoS) on top of kernel cgroup enforcement. It balances extensibility (via topology hints, device plugins, custom policies) with operational simplicity (stateful allocation, automatic cleanup). Platform differences (Linux cgroup v1/v2 vs. Windows Job Objects) are abstracted behind interfaces. The critical flow is pod admission → resource allocation → cgroup creation → container creation → periodic reconciliation, with failure handling through checkpointing and garbage collection.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3503,"cache_read_input_tokens":91704,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3503},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b6cfd4c6-3407-46b3-8c9a-e7eced3ba83b","uuid":"a0c64b90-dce3-40f3-a8ab-baa90390ca0e"}

Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe container manager is the core subsystem responsible for managing compute resource allocation, enforcement, and lifecycle on a node. It acts as the orchestration layer between the kubelet's pod synchronization logic and the underlying kernel resource control mechanisms (cgroups), container runtime (CRI), and specialized resource controllers.\n\n### Core Responsibilities\n- **Resource enforcement**: Apply CPU, memory, and device quotas to containers via cgroups\n- **Hierarchical QoS management**: Organize pods into Guaranteed, Burstable, and BestEffort cgroups\n- **Node allocatable enforcement**: Reserve resources for system and kubelet components\n- **Resource coordination**: Align CPU, memory, and device allocations with NUMA topology\n- **Plugin integration**: Manage device plugins and device memory allocation\n- **Dynamic resource lifecycle**: Support runtime preparation/unpreperation of extended resources (DRA)\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n- **Pod & Node APIs** (`k8s.io/api/core/v1`): Pod specifications, resource requests/limits, QoS class\n- **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)** (`k8s.io/cri-api`): Container lifecycle, resource updates\n- **cAdvisor** (`k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/kubelet/cadvisor`): Machine topology, capacity discovery\n- **Status Provider**: Pod status tracking from runtime\n- **Events**: Node event recording for warnings/errors\n\n### Downstream Dependencies\n- **Kubelet's pod workers** (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`): Trigger pod admission and synchronization\n- **Lifecycle admission handlers** (`pkg/kubelet/lifecycle`): Enforce pod admission constraints\n- **Pod resources API** (`pkg/kubelet/apis/podresources`): Expose allocated resources to external consumers\n- **Container runtime**: Actual container creation and resource enforcement\n- **cgroups filesystem**: Linux kernel resource limiting mechanism\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Separation\n\n### 2.1 ContainerManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go)\n\nThe primary interface implemented by `containerManagerImpl` defines the contract for all container management operations:\n\n```go\ntype ContainerManager interface {\n    Start(context.Context, *v1.Node, ActivePodsFunc, GetNodeFunc, ...) error\n    SystemCgroupsLimit() v1.ResourceList\n    GetNodeConfig() NodeConfig\n    Status() Status\n    NewPodContainerManager() PodContainerManager\n    GetMountedSubsystems() *CgroupSubsystems\n    GetQOSContainersInfo() QOSContainersInfo\n    GetNodeAllocatableReservation() v1.ResourceList\n    GetCapacity(localStorageCapacityIsolation bool) v1.ResourceList\n    UpdateQOSCgroups(logger klog.Logger) error\n    GetResources(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) (*RunContainerOptions, error)\n    GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler() lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler\n    InternalContainerLifecycle() InternalContainerLifecycle\n    PrepareDynamicResources(context.Context, *v1.Pod) error\n    UnprepareDynamicResources(context.Context, *v1.Pod) error\n    // ... additional methods for device tracking, exclusive CPUs, topology hints\n}\n```\n\n**Key responsibility**: Orchestrates initialization and maintains references to all sub-managers.\n\n### 2.2 containerManagerImpl (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go)\n\nThe Linux-specific implementation manages the lifecycle and coordination of six core sub-systems:\n\n| Component | Role | File |\n|-----------|------|------|\n| **CgroupManager** | Abstracts cgroup v1/v2 operations (create, update, destroy cgroups) | `cgroup_manager_linux.go` |\n| **QOSContainerManager** | Creates and maintains QoS-tier cgroup hierarchy | `qos_container_manager_linux.go` |\n| **CPU Manager** | Allocates CPU affinity based on policy (static/none) | `cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` |\n| **Memory Manager** | Allocates NUMA-local memory for guaranteed pods | `memorymanager/memory_manager.go` |\n| **Device Manager** | Manages device plugin allocations | `devicemanager/manager.go` |\n| **Topology Manager** | Coordinates NUMA-aware resource alignment | `topologymanager/topology_manager.go` |\n| **DRA Manager** | Handles Dynamic Resource Allocation (optional feature) | `dra/manager.go` |\n\n**State in containerManagerImpl**:\n```go\ntype containerManagerImpl struct {\n    sync.RWMutex\n    NodeConfig                      // Configuration: cgroup paths, policies, limits\n    cadvisorInterface               // Machine topology and capacity discovery\n    cgroupManager CgroupManager      // Low-level cgroup operations\n    qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager\n    deviceManager devicemanager.Manager\n    cpuManager cpumanager.Manager\n    memoryManager memorymanager.Manager\n    topologyManager topologymanager.Manager\n    draManager *dra.Manager\n    capacity, internalCapacity v1.ResourceList\n    cgroupRoot CgroupName            // Root cgroup for all pods\n    systemContainers []*systemContainer  // Kubelet, system services\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 PodContainerManager Interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go)\n\nAbstracts pod-level cgroup management, enabling the two-tier hierarchy (QoS tier → pod tier → container tier):\n\n```go\ntype PodContainerManager interface {\n    GetPodContainerName(*v1.Pod) (CgroupName, string)\n    EnsureExists(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\n    Exists(*v1.Pod) bool\n    Destroy(logger klog.Logger, name CgroupName) error\n    ReduceCPULimits(logger klog.Logger, name CgroupName) error\n    GetAllPodsFromCgroups() (map[types.UID]CgroupName, error)\n    IsPodCgroup(cgroupfs string) (bool, types.UID)\n    GetPodCgroupMemoryUsage(pod *v1.Pod) (uint64, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation**: `podContainerManagerImpl` (pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go)\n- Maps pod UID → cgroup under appropriate QoS tier\n- Creates pod cgroup during pod admission\n- Configures CPU/memory QoS parameters per pod\n\n### 2.4 Resource Managers\n\n#### CPU Manager (pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go)\n\n**Purpose**: Allocate exclusive CPUs to containers requesting them.\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Start(ctx context.Context, activePods ActivePodsFunc, sourcesReady config.SourcesReady,\n          podStatusProvider status.PodStatusProvider, containerRuntime runtimeService,\n          initialContainers containermap.ContainerMap) error\n    Allocate(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) error\n    AddContainer(logger logr.Logger, p *v1.Pod, c *v1.Container, containerID string)\n    RemoveContainer(logger logr.Logger, containerID string) error\n    State() state.Reader\n    GetTopologyHints(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n    GetExclusiveCPUs(podUID, containerName string) cpuset.CPUSet\n    GetAllocatableCPUs() cpuset.CPUSet\n}\n```\n\n**Policies**:\n- **None** (`policy_none.go`): No CPU pinning; all containers share the shared pool\n- **Static** (`policy_static.go`): Exclusive CPU allocation with optional NUMA/socket alignment\n\n**State persistence**: Checkpointed to `cpu_manager_state` file (kubelet root dir)\n\n#### Memory Manager (pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go)\n\n**Purpose**: Allocate NUMA-local memory to guaranteed pods.\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Start(ctx context.Context, activePods ActivePodsFunc, sourcesReady config.SourcesReady,\n          podStatusProvider status.PodStatusProvider, containerRuntime runtimeService,\n          initialContainers containermap.ContainerMap) error\n    AddContainer(logger klog.Logger, p *v1.Pod, c *v1.Container, containerID string)\n    Allocate(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) error\n    RemoveContainer(logger klog.Logger, containerID string) error\n    State() state.Reader\n    GetTopologyHints(*v1.Pod, *v1.Container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n    GetMemoryNUMANodes(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) sets.Set[int]\n    GetAllocatableMemory() []state.Block\n}\n```\n\n**Policies**:\n- **None**: No special memory allocation\n- **Static**: Allocates memory from isolated NUMA nodes per container, only for guaranteed containers\n\n#### Device Manager (pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/)\n\n**Purpose**: Enumerate device plugins, allocate devices to containers, collect topology hints.\n\n**Key methods**:\n- `Start(ctx)`: Discover and manage device plugin endpoints\n- `Allocate(ctx, pod, container) error`: Call device plugin Allocate RPC\n- `GetDeviceRunContainerOptions(ctx, pod, container)`: Return CDI devices, mounts, envs for runtime\n- `GetTopologyHints(pod, container)`: Provide NUMA alignment hints\n- `UpdateAllocatedDevices()`: Release devices from terminated pods\n\n**Device plugins** communicate via Unix socket following the Kubernetes device plugin protocol.\n\n#### Topology Manager (pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/)\n\n**Purpose**: Coordinate NUMA topology hints from CPU, memory, and device managers during pod admission.\n\n**Policies**:\n- **None**: No topology awareness (default)\n- **Best-Effort**: Collect hints but allow pod admission regardless\n- **Restricted**: Reject pod if no topology hint can satisfy all managers\n- **Single-NUMA-Node**: Reject pod if resources cannot be allocated from a single NUMA node\n\n**Admission flow**:\n1. Pod admission handler calls `Admit(pod, attributes)`\n2. Topology manager queries `GetTopologyHints(pod, container)` for each manager\n3. Evaluates policy and either approves or rejects the pod\n\n### 2.5 CgroupManager (pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go, cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go, cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go)\n\n**Purpose**: Abstract cgroup v1 vs. v2 implementation differences.\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype CgroupManager interface {\n    Create(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Destroy(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Update(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Exists(name CgroupName) bool\n    Pids(logger klog.Logger, name CgroupName) []int\n    MemoryUsage(name CgroupName) (int64, error)\n    Version() int  // 1 or 2\n}\n```\n\n**CgroupConfig** specifies:\n```go\ntype CgroupConfig struct {\n    Name CgroupName  // e.g., []string{\"kubepods\", \"burstable\", \"pod-abc-123\"}\n    ResourceParameters *ResourceConfig\n}\n```\n\n**ResourceConfig** holds:\n- Memory limit (bytes)\n- CPU set (pinning)\n- CPU shares (relative weight)\n- CPU quota/period (CFS bandwidth limiting)\n- PIDs limit\n- Cgroup v2 unified dict for memory QoS, etc.\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Container Manager Initialization\n\n**File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:NewContainerManager()` (line 207)**\n\n```\n1. Validate cgroup subsystems mounted (cpu, memory, cpuset at minimum)\n   ↓\n2. Get machine info from cAdvisor (topology, capacity)\n   ↓\n3. Create CgroupManager (v1 or v2 driver)\n   ↓\n4. Validate and set cgroup root (e.g., /kubepods)\n   ↓\n5. Create QOSContainerManager\n   └─ Initializes three QoS tier cgroups:\n      - guaranteed: high priority, strict isolation\n      - burstable: medium priority, shared CPU shares\n      - besteffort: low priority, shared resources\n   ↓\n6. Create Topology Manager (with policy)\n   ↓\n7. Create Device Manager\n   ├─ Scan /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins for sockets\n   └─ Establish watch connection for device updates\n   ↓\n8. Create CPU Manager (with policy and reserved CPUs)\n   └─ Reconciliation loop monitors container CPU affinity\n   ↓\n9. Create Memory Manager (with policy and NUMA info)\n   └─ Tracks memory allocation state for guaranteed pods\n   ↓\n10. Register CPU/Memory/Device as Topology Manager hint providers\n   ↓\n11. Create resource updates channel\n    └─ Fan-in updates from device and DRA managers\n```\n\n**Result**: `containerManagerImpl` ready for `Start()` call during kubelet startup.\n\n### 3.2 Pod Admission Flow\n\n**Trigger**: Kubelet receives new pod; calls `NewLifecycleManager().Admit(pod, attributes)`\n\n**File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` (line 760)**\nReturns `topologyManager` as the admission handler.\n\n**Flow**:\n\n```\nPod arrives at kubelet\n   ↓\n→ Topology Manager Admit()\n   ├─ For each container in pod:\n   │  ├─ Call CPU Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n   │  ├─ Call Memory Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n   │  └─ Call Device Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n   │\n   ├─ Apply topology policy:\n   │  ├─ Collect hints from all managers\n   │  ├─ Find best alignment (if restricted policy)\n   │  └─ Reject pod if no alignment possible (restricted/single-numa-node)\n   │\n   └─ If approved:\n      ├─ Pod advances to pod worker\n      └─ Pod worker calls Allocate() during SyncPod\n   ↓\n→ Pod Worker SyncPod()\n   └─ Calls containerManager.GetResources() per container\n      ├─ DRA Manager.GetResources(pod, container) → CDI devices\n      └─ Device Manager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions(pod, container)\n         → Devices, Mounts, Env vars, Annotations, CDI devices\n   ↓\n→ Resource Allocation Calls\n   ├─ CPU Manager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   │  └─ State: Record (pod UID, container name) → CPUSet\n   ├─ Memory Manager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   │  └─ State: Record pod UID → NUMA node allocation\n   └─ Device Manager.Allocate(pod, container)\n      └─ RPC to device plugin: AllocateRequest → AllocateResponse\n   ↓\n→ Container Creation\n   └─ Runtime receives RunContainerOptions with allocated resources\n      ├─ CPU affinity set via CRI ContainerConfig\n      ├─ Devices passed via RunOptions\n      └─ Env vars injected for device paths\n```\n\n### 3.3 Container Lifecycle Management\n\n**File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`**\n\nThe `InternalContainerLifecycle` provides hooks called at critical points:\n\n```\nContainer being created\n   ↓\n→ InternalContainerLifecycle.PreCreateContainer()\n   ├─ Called during CreateContainer in kuberuntime\n   └─ Not currently used for resource managers\n   ↓\n→ Container created successfully\n   ↓\n→ InternalContainerLifecycle.PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   ├─ CPU Manager.AddContainer(logger, pod, container, containerID)\n   │  └─ Maps containerID → (pod UID, container name) for later reconciliation\n   ├─ Memory Manager.AddContainer(logger, pod, container, containerID)\n   │  └─ Registers container in memory allocation tracking\n   └─ Topology Manager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n      └─ Registers container for topology state tracking\n   ↓\n→ Container runs\n   ↓\n→ Container terminated\n   ↓\n→ InternalContainerLifecycle.PostStopContainer(containerID)\n   └─ Topology Manager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      └─ Cleanup topology state\n   ↓\n→ Background: CPU/Memory managers remove container during reconciliation\n   ├─ CPU Manager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n   │  └─ Release CPUs back to shared pool\n   └─ Memory Manager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n      └─ Release NUMA node allocations\n```\n\n### 3.4 QoS Cgroup Hierarchy Creation\n\n**File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:setupNode()` (line 504)**\n\nDuring `Start()`, if `CgroupsPerQOS` is enabled:\n\n```\nStart()\n   ↓\n→ setupNode(ctx, activePods)\n   ├─ Validate cgroup subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset, etc.)\n   ├─ Setup kernel tunables (sysctl)\n   ├─ createNodeAllocatableCgroups()\n   │  └─ Create cgroup under user-specified cgroup-root\n   │     └─ (e.g., /kubepods under /sys/fs/cgroup/)\n   │\n   ├─ qosContainerManager.Start()\n   │  └─ Create three QoS tier cgroups\n   │     ├─ /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/.../kubepods/guaranteed\n   │     ├─ /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/.../kubepods/burstable\n   │     └─ /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/.../kubepods/besteffort\n   │\n   ├─ enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()\n   │  └─ Set limits on each QoS tier based on:\n   │     ├─ Node capacity\n   │     ├─ Node allocatable\n   │     └─ QoS reserved settings\n   │\n   └─ Setup system containers (Kubelet, system services)\n      └─ Ensure kubelet process in designated cgroup\n```\n\n**Cgroup hierarchy structure**:\n```\n/kubepods                                     # Node allocatable enforcement\n├─ guaranteed/                                # Guaranteed pods\n│  └─ pod-<uid>/                              # Individual pod\n│     ├─ <container1>/                        # Individual container\n│     └─ <container2>/\n├─ burstable/\n│  └─ pod-<uid>/\n│     └─ <containers>/\n└─ besteffort/\n   └─ pod-<uid>/\n      └─ <containers>/\n```\n\n### 3.5 Pod Synchronization (SyncPod)\n\n**Simplified flow during pod worker's SyncPod() call:**\n\n```\nSyncPod(pod)\n   ↓\n→ Ensure pod container created\n   ├─ Get PodContainerManager from containerManager\n   │  (returns podContainerManagerImpl)\n   │\n   ├─ podContainerManager.EnsureExists(pod)\n   │  ├─ Determine pod QoS class (Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort)\n   │  ├─ Get parent QoS cgroup (guaranteed/burstable/besteffort)\n   │  └─ Create pod cgroup under parent:\n   │     └─ cgroupManager.Create(logger, &CgroupConfig{\n   │        Name: NewCgroupName(parentQoS, \"pod-<uid>\"),\n   │        ResourceParameters: ResourceConfigForPod(pod, ...),\n   │     })\n   │     ├─ CPU limits: Based on requests and CPU manager policy\n   │     ├─ Memory limits: Based on memory requests\n   │     └─ CPU/Memory QoS params: If MemoryQoS feature enabled\n   │\n   └─ For each container in pod:\n      ├─ Allocate resources (CPU, memory, devices)\n      ├─ Get container runtime options\n      │  └─ containerManager.GetResources(ctx, pod, container)\n      │     ├─ draManager.GetResources() → CDI devices\n      │     └─ deviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions() → Devices/Mounts/Env\n      │\n      └─ Create container with runtime\n         └─ Container runtime applies:\n            ├─ CPU affinity (from CPU Manager)\n            ├─ Memory limits and NUMA policy\n            ├─ Device mounts and CDI devices\n            └─ Environment variables from device manager\n```\n\n### 3.6 Resource Reconciliation\n\n**CPU Manager Reconciliation** (runs periodically):\n\n```\nEvery CPUManagerReconcilePeriod (default: 200ms)\n   ↓\n→ cpuManager reconciles current state\n   ├─ Get active pods from activePods()\n   ├─ For each running container:\n   │  ├─ Read desired CPU set from state\n   │  ├─ Get actual CPU set from cgroup (cpuset.cpus)\n   │  ├─ If mismatch:\n   │  │  └─ Update via runtimeService.UpdateContainerResources()\n   │  │     └─ CRI call to container runtime to apply CPU affinity\n   │  └─ Update container's CPU period/quota if needed\n   │\n   └─ Enforce allocatable reservation (reserved CPUs stay isolated)\n```\n\n**Memory Manager Reconciliation**:\n```\nOn startup and periodically\n   ↓\n→ memoryManager reconciles\n   ├─ Load state from checkpoint file (memory_manager_state)\n   ├─ For each running guaranteed pod:\n   │  └─ Verify memory allocation matches state\n   │\n   └─ Call runtimeService.UpdateContainerResources() if needed\n      └─ Apply memory limits and NUMA policies\n```\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n| Scenario | Impact | Mitigation |\n|----------|--------|-----------|\n| **Cgroup subsystem not mounted** | Container manager fails to initialize | Kubelet startup error; operator must enable cgroups |\n| **Swap enabled on node** | Memory limits not enforced; pod eviction may fail | `--fail-swap-on=true` (default) prevents kubelet start, or warning issued |\n| **CPU quota period unsupported** | CPU hardcapping unavailable | Status.SoftRequirements reports error; kubelet still starts |\n| **Device plugin crashes** | Containers can't allocate devices | Device allocation fails; pod admission rejected if devices required |\n| **NUMA topology detection fails** | Topology manager can't provide hints | Topology manager reverts to \"none\" policy; pod admission succeeds without alignment |\n| **Cgroup v1 to v2 migration** | Old state not readable in new hierarchy | CPUManager/MemoryManager state files incompatible; state must be cleared |\n| **Container removed without notification** | Resource leak (CPUs, memory, devices) | Periodic reconciliation detects orphaned resources and cleans up |\n| **Kubelet restart while pod running** | State loss; resources may be re-allocated | Checkpoints persisted to disk; restored on startup |\n\n### 4.2 Resource Limits and Constraints\n\n| Limit | Default | Tunable | Impact |\n|-------|---------|---------|--------|\n| **Pod PIDs limit** | Unbounded | `--pod-pids-limit` | Prevents fork bombs at pod level |\n| **CPU CFS quota period** | 100ms | `--cpu-cfs-quota-period` | Too low: scheduler overhead; too high: coarse granularity |\n| **CPU Manager reconcile period** | 200ms | `--cpu-manager-reconcile-period` | Tradeoff between responsiveness and overhead |\n| **Topology Manager scope** | container | `--topology-manager-scope=pod` | Pod scope: stricter alignment but higher rejection rate |\n| **Device manager max devices per pod** | No hard limit | Plugin-dependent | Device availability is soft limit |\n| **Memory allocatable reservation** | Computed from allocatable | Per-NUMA manual reservation | Prevents overallocation on NUMA nodes |\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### 3.3.1 Stateful Resource Allocation vs. Runtime State\n\n**Tradeoff**: CPU and Memory managers maintain state on disk (checkpoint files).\n- **Advantage**: Survive kubelet restart; container resources not lost\n- **Disadvantage**: State can become stale; requires garbage collection on pod cleanup\n- **Evidence**: `cpu_manager_state`, `memory_manager_state` files in kubelet root directory\n\n#### 3.3.2 Topology Hints vs. Hard NUMA Binding\n\n**Tradeoff**: Topology manager collects hints; final NUMA decision made during runtime.UpdateContainerResources().\n- **Advantage**: Resource managers can express preferences; runtime (e.g., containerd) applies best policy\n- **Disadvantage**: Hints can be ignored by runtime; containers may not get optimal NUMA locality\n- **Evidence**: `topologymanager/policy_*.go` provide hints; CPU/Memory managers don't directly set NUMA masks\n\n#### 3.3.3 Per-Pod vs. Per-Container Resource Management\n\n**Tradeoff**: Kubelet enforces pod-level cgroup limits; per-container limits via cgroup limits.\n- **Advantage**: Pod-level QoS applies across all containers; simpler admission\n- **Disadvantage**: Container-level oversubscription possible (e.g., 2 containers each requesting 500m CPU in 1CPU pod)\n- **Evidence**: `podContainerManagerImpl.EnsureExists()` creates pod cgroup; CPUs allocated per-container\n\n#### 3.3.4 Exclusive CPU Allocation and Shared Pool\n\n**Tradeoff**: Static CPU policy allocates exclusive CPUs to some containers; others share.\n- **Advantage**: Deterministic latency for latency-sensitive workloads (exclusive)\n- **Disadvantage**: CPU fragmentation; shared pool may be underutilized or overloaded\n- **Evidence**: `cpumanager/policy_static.go` tracks exclusive set; others use shared pool\n\n#### 3.3.5 Device Plugin Protocol vs. Built-in Device Support\n\n**Tradeoff**: Devices managed via out-of-process plugins (Unix sockets).\n- **Advantage**: Extensibility; new device types without kubelet changes\n- **Disadvantage**: Plugin crashes impact availability; state not persisted in kubelet\n- **Evidence**: Device manager scans `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/` for sockets; allocations stored in memory only\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Policy Customization\n\n#### CPU Manager Policies\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go`\n\nImplement `Policy` interface:\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start(cpuDetails CPUDetails, systemReserved, kubeReserved cpuset.CPUSet) error\n    AddContainer(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container, containerID string) error\n    RemoveContainer(containerID string) error\n    GetExclusiveCPUs(podUID, containerName string) cpuset.CPUSet\n    GetTopologyHints(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n}\n```\n\n**Builtin policies**:\n- `policy_none.go`: All containers share CPUs\n- `policy_static.go`: Guaranteed pods with integer CPU requests get exclusive CPUs\n\n**Extension**: Add new policy by implementing `Policy` interface and registering in `NewManager()` switch statement.\n\n#### Memory Manager Policies\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy.go`\n\nImplement `Policy` interface:\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start(guaranteedPods []*v1.Pod) error\n    AddContainer(logger logr.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container, containerID string) error\n    RemoveContainer(logger logr.Logger, containerID string) error\n    GetTopologyHints(...) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n}\n```\n\n**Builtin policies**:\n- `policy_none.go`: No memory pinning\n- `policy_static.go`: NUMA-local allocation for guaranteed pods\n\n#### Topology Manager Policies\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy.go`\n\nImplement `Manager` interface (admission, hint aggregation).\n\n**Builtin policies**:\n- `policy_none.go`: No topology awareness\n- `policy_best_effort.go`: Collect hints but allow pod regardless\n- `policy_restricted.go`: Reject pod if hints don't align\n- `policy_single_numa_node.go`: Restrict to single NUMA node\n\n### 5.2 Topology Manager Hint Provider Registration\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:NewContainerManager()` (line 296–356)\n\nAny component implementing `topologymanager.HintProvider` can register:\n\n```go\ncm.topologyManager.AddHintProvider(logger, deviceManager)\ncm.topologyManager.AddHintProvider(logger, cpuManager)\ncm.topologyManager.AddHintProvider(logger, memoryManager)\n```\n\n**How to add new provider**:\n1. Implement `GetTopologyHints(pod, container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint`\n2. Call `topologyManager.AddHintProvider()` in container manager initialization\n3. Topology manager queries your provider during pod admission\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugin Integration\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/`\n\nDevice plugins communicate via gRPC over Unix socket:\n\n```protobuf\nservice DevicePlugin {\n    rpc ListAndWatch(Empty) returns (stream ListAndWatchResponse);\n    rpc Allocate(AllocateRequest) returns (AllocateResponse);\n    rpc PreStartContainer(PreStartContainerRequest) returns (PreStartContainerResponse);\n    rpc GetDeviceRunContainerOptions(GetDeviceRunContainerOptionsRequest) returns (GetDeviceRunContainerOptionsResponse);\n    rpc GetPreferredAllocation(GetPreferredAllocationRequest) returns (GetPreferredAllocationResponse);\n}\n```\n\n**Extension**: Write a device plugin that listens on `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/<plugin_name>.sock` and implements the protocol.\n\n### 5.4 Runtime Service Updates\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`, `memorymanager/memory_manager.go`\n\nManagers call:\n```go\nruntimeService.UpdateContainerResources(ctx, containerID, &runtimeapi.ContainerResources{\n    CPUPeriod: period,\n    CPUQuota:  quota,\n    CPUSetCpus: cpuSetStr,\n    MemoryLimitInBytes: memLimit,\n    MemorySwapLimitInBytes: swapLimit,\n    // ... other fields\n})\n```\n\n**Extension**: Kubelet's runtime interface supports any CRI-compatible runtime (containerd, cri-o, etc.). Resource updates are propagated to the runtime, which applies them to the container.\n\n### 5.5 Kubelet's Pod Admit Handler Chain\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/admission.go`\n\nContainer manager's `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns the topology manager, which is consulted during pod admission:\n\n```go\nhandlers := []lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler{\n    cm.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler(), // Topology manager\n    // ... other handlers (secrets, volumes, etc.)\n}\n```\n\n**Extension**: Custom admission handlers can be registered in the kubelet's admission chain (outside container manager scope, but coordinates with it).\n\n## 6. Platform Variance\n\n### 6.1 Linux vs. Windows\n\n**Linux**: Full cgroup-based resource enforcement via containerManagerImpl (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go)\n- Cgroups v1 and v2 support\n- CPU manager and memory manager support\n- QoS cgroup hierarchy\n- NUMA and device topology support\n\n**Windows**: Minimal stub implementation (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go)\n- No cgroup support (Windows uses Job Objects instead)\n- CPU/memory managers still initialized but operate on Job Object limits\n- Topology manager and device manager functional\n- No QoS cgroup hierarchy\n\n### 6.2 Cgroup v1 vs. v2\n\n**Cgroup v1** (legacy):\n- Separate subsystems: cpu, cpuacct, memory, cpuset, pids\n- Kubelet validates each subsystem mounted\n- Files: cpu.shares, cpu.cfs_quota_us, memory.limit_in_bytes, cpuset.cpus\n\n**Cgroup v2** (unified):\n- Single hierarchy with all controllers\n- Kubelet detects via `cgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode()`\n- Files: cpu.max, memory.max, cpuset.cpus\n- Automatic memory QoS via memory.oom.group and memory.pressure_level\n\n**Handling**: CgroupManager abstraction hides v1/v2 differences\n- `cgroup_manager_linux.go`: Detects version\n- `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`: v1-specific logic\n- `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`: v2-specific logic\n\n### 6.3 CPU Hard Capping\n\n**Feature flag**: `CPUHardcapping`\n\nIf CPU CFS quota unavailable (old kernel or cgroup v1 cpu subsystem missing):\n- Kubelet detects during `validateSystemRequirements()`\n- Sets `status.SoftRequirements` error\n- Kubelet still starts but CPU limits not enforced\n- Users must manually manage CPU affinity\n\n### 6.4 Memory QoS\n\n**Feature flag**: `MemoryQoS` (requires cgroup v2)\n\n**Behavior**:\n```go\nif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(kubefeatures.MemoryQoS) &&\n   libcontainercgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode() {\n    // Apply memory QoS parameters\n    // E.g., memory.min, memory.low, memory.oom.group\n}\n```\n\nOptimizes OOM behavior for guaranteed vs. burstable pods.\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance Considerations\n\n#### CPU Manager Overhead\n- Reconciliation runs every `cpu-manager-reconcile-period` (default 200ms)\n- Cost: Iterating active pods, reading cgroup state, CRI UpdateContainerResources() calls\n- Mitigation: Set reconciliation period based on workload sensitivity (higher period for batch workloads)\n\n#### Topology Manager Admission Latency\n- Pod admission time increases with number of containers and NUMA nodes\n- Complexity grows in `restricted` and `single-numa-node` policies\n- Mitigation: Use `best-effort` for large clusters; reserve topology-sensitive pods for dedicated nodes\n\n#### Device Manager Scalability\n- Device plugins communicate synchronously with kubelet\n- Large number of devices per container → longer Allocate() RPC time\n- Mitigation: Device plugins should implement PreferredAllocation() to minimize allocation rounds\n\n### 7.2 Reliability and Recovery\n\n#### Checkpoint Persistence\n- CPU and Memory managers write state to disk after each change\n- **Location**: `${kubelet-root-dir}/cpu_manager_state`, `memory_manager_state`\n- **Recovery**: On kubelet restart, state is restored from checkpoint\n- **Risk**: If checkpoint corrupted, manually delete and kubelet will re-allocate from runtime state\n\n#### Orphaned Resource Cleanup\n- If container dies without notifying kubelet, resources may be allocated in cgroup but not tracked\n- **Detection**: Periodic reconciliation compares runtime pods with cgroup state\n- **Cleanup**: Garbage collection removes resources from orphaned cgroups\n\n#### Device Plugin Tolerance\n- If device plugin crashes, existing pod allocations persisted in kubelet state\n- New pods cannot allocate from crashed plugin\n- **Recovery**: Restart device plugin; kubelet re-establishes connection\n\n### 7.3 Monitoring and Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics\n- `kubelet_cgroup_manager_duration_seconds`: Time to create/update cgroups\n- `kubelet_pod_worker_duration_seconds`: Pod synchronization time (includes resource allocation)\n- `kubelet_device_manager_alloc_duration_seconds`: Device allocation latency\n- `kubelet_cpu_manager_reconcile_duration_seconds`: CPU manager reconciliation time\n\n#### Logs to Monitor\n- Look for \"Failed to allocate CPU\" → CPU exhaustion or allocation errors\n- Look for \"topology manager policy violation\" → Pod rejected due to NUMA constraints\n- Look for \"device plugin endpoint not found\" → Device plugin startup issues\n\n### 7.4 Configuration Best Practices\n\n| Setting | Recommendation | Rationale |\n|---------|-----------------|-----------|\n| `--cpu-manager-policy=static` | Only for latency-sensitive workloads | Overhead is minimal; helps predictable latency |\n| `--memory-manager-policy=static` | Only if NUMA allocation critical | Adds memory pinning overhead |\n| `--topology-manager-policy=restricted` | For co-located workloads needing alignment | Restrictive; use `best-effort` for flexibility |\n| `--pod-pids-limit=4096` | Set per node based on workload | Prevents fork bombs; reduce for untrusted multi-tenant |\n| `--cgroups-per-qos=true` | Recommended for multi-tenant clusters | Enables QoS isolation; always enable |\n| `--enforce-node-allocatable=pods,kube-reserved,system-reserved` | Strict enforcement | Prevents kubelet/system starvation |\n\n## 8. File and Directory Reference Map\n\n### Core Container Manager\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` | ContainerManager interface definition |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` | Linux implementation; initialization, lifecycle, orchestration |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` | Windows stub implementation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` | Shared types: CgroupConfig, ResourceConfig, PodContainerManager |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` | Pod-level cgroup management |\n\n### Cgroup Management\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` | Main cgroup manager; driver selection |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` | Cgroup v1 operations |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` | Cgroup v2 operations |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` | QoS tier cgroup creation/management |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/node_container_manager_linux.go` | Node-level cgroup enforcement |\n\n### Resource Managers\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` | CPU allocation interface and manager implementation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy*.go` | CPU allocation policies (none, static) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/state/` | CPU allocation state persistence |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go` | Memory allocation interface and manager |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy*.go` | Memory allocation policies (none, static) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go` | Device plugin integration |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go` | NUMA topology coordination |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy*.go` | Topology policies (none, best-effort, restricted, single-numa-node) |\n\n### Lifecycle Hooks\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` | Hooks for container lifecycle (PreStart, PostStop) |\n\n### DRA (Dynamic Resource Allocation)\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/` | Dynamic resource allocation manager |\n\n### Interfaces and Contracts\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go` | Runtime interface (pod/container status, lifecycle) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/` | Pod admission lifecycle hooks |\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe kubelet container manager is a layered architecture orchestrating resource allocation through six specialized sub-systems (CPU, Memory, Device, Topology, DRA, QoS) on top of kernel cgroup enforcement. It balances extensibility (via topology hints, device plugins, custom policies) with operational simplicity (stateful allocation, automatic cleanup). Platform differences (Linux cgroup v1/v2 vs. Windows Job Objects) are abstracted behind interfaces. The critical flow is pod admission → resource allocation → cgroup creation → container creation → periodic reconciliation, with failure handling through checkpointing and garbage collection.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe container manager is the core subsystem responsible for managing compute resource allocation, enforcement, and lifecycle on a node. It acts as the orchestration layer between the kubelet's pod synchronization logic and the underlying kernel resource control mechanisms (cgroups), container runtime (CRI), and specialized resource controllers.\n\n### Core Responsibilities\n- **Resource enforcement**: Apply CPU, memory, and device quotas to containers via cgroups\n- **Hierarchical QoS management**: Organize pods into Guaranteed, Burstable, and BestEffort cgroups\n- **Node allocatable enforcement**: Reserve resources for system and kubelet components\n- **Resource coordination**: Align CPU, memory, and device allocations with NUMA topology\n- **Plugin integration**: Manage device plugins and device memory allocation\n- **Dynamic resource lifecycle**: Support runtime preparation/unpreperation of extended resources (DRA)\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n- **Pod & Node APIs** (`k8s.io/api/core/v1`): Pod specifications, resource requests/limits, QoS class\n- **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)** (`k8s.io/cri-api`): Container lifecycle, resource updates\n- **cAdvisor** (`k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/kubelet/cadvisor`): Machine topology, capacity discovery\n- **Status Provider**: Pod status tracking from runtime\n- **Events**: Node event recording for warnings/errors\n\n### Downstream Dependencies\n- **Kubelet's pod workers** (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`): Trigger pod admission and synchronization\n- **Lifecycle admission handlers** (`pkg/kubelet/lifecycle`): Enforce pod admission constraints\n- **Pod resources API** (`pkg/kubelet/apis/podresources`): Expose allocated resources to external consumers\n- **Container runtime**: Actual container creation and resource enforcement\n- **cgroups filesystem**: Linux kernel resource limiting mechanism\n\n## 2. InternalContainerLifecycle() InternalContainerLifecycle\n    PrepareDynamicResources(context.Context, *v1.Pod) error\n    UnprepareDynamicResources(context.Context, *v1.Pod) error\n    // ...
